# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've identified all the key Go source files implementing the alert notification pipeline:

**Core Components:**
1. **Alert Ingestion** - `api/v2/api.go:postAlertsHandler` receives alerts via HTTP API
2. **Routing/Dispatch** - `dispatch/dispatch.go` manages alert subscription and processes alerts through the routing tree
3. **Routing Tree Traversal** - `dispatch/route.go:Route.Match` performs depth-first search through routing rules
4. **Inhibition Check** - `inhibit/inhibit.go:Inhibitor.Mutes` evaluates inhibition rules
5. **Silence Check** - `silence/silence.go:Silencer.Mutes` checks for silenced alerts
6. **Notification Pipeline** - `notify/notify.go` orchestrates the complete pipeline with stages:
   - MuteStage (inhibition and silence filtering)
   - DedupStage (deduplication via notification log)
   - RetryStage (notification delivery with retry logic)
   - FanoutStage (parallel execution across receivers)

The answer.json file contains the complete list of files, symbols, execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining how alerts flow through the entire system from ingestion to final dispatch.

{\\n128: \\t\\t\\t// Super fast path: No silences ever applied to this\\n129: \\t\\t\\t// alert, none have been added. \\t}\\n174: \\ts.logger.Debug(\\n175: \\t\\t\\\"determined current silences state\\\",\\n176: \\t\\t\\\"now\\\", now,\\n177: \\t\\t\\\"total\\\", len(allSils),\\n178: \\t\\t\\\"active\\\", {\\n596: \\ts.mtx.Lock()\\n597: \\tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\\n598: \\n599: \\tnow := s.nowUTC()\\n600: \\tif sil.StartsAt.IsZero() {\\n601: \\t\\tsil.StartsAt = now\\n602: \\t}\\n603: \\n604: \\tif err := Muter interface.\n113: func (s *Silencer) Mutes(lset model.LabelSet) bool {\n114: \tfp := lset.Fingerprint()\n115: \tactiveIDs, pendingIDs, markerVersion, _ := s.marker.Silenced(fp)\n116: \n117: \tvar (\n118: \t\terr        error\n119: \t\tallSils    []*pb.Silence\n120: \t\tnewVersion = markerVersion\n121: \t)\n122: \tif markerVersion == s.silences.Version() {\n123: \t\ttotalSilences := len(activeIDs) + len(pendingIDs)\n124: \t\t// No new silences added, just need to check which of the old\n125: \t\t// silences are still relevant and which of the pending ones\n126: \t\t// have become active.\n127: \t\tif totalSilences == 0 {\n128: \t\t\t// Super fast path: No silences ever applied to this\n129: \t\t\t// alert, none have been added. We are done.\n130: \t\t\treturn false\n131: \t\t}\n132: \t\t// This is still a quite fast path: No silences have been added,\n133: \t\t// we only need to check which of the applicable silences are\n134: \t\t// currently active. Note that newVersion is left at\n135: \t\t// markerVersion because the Query call might already return a\n136: \t\t// newer version, which is not the version our old list of\n137: \t\t// applicable silences is based on.\n138: \t\tallIDs := append(append(make([]string, 0, totalSilences), activeIDs...), pendingIDs...)\n139: \t\tallSils, _, err = s.silences.Query(\n140: \t\t\tQIDs(allIDs...),\n141: \t\t\tQState(types.SilenceStateActive, types.SilenceStatePending),\n142: \t\t)\n143: \t} else {\n144: \t\t// New silences have been added, do a full query.\n145: \t\tallSils, newVersion, err = s.silences.Query(\n146: \t\t\tQState(types.SilenceStateActive, types.SilenceStatePending),\n147: \t\t\tQMatches(lset),\n148: \t\t)\n149: \t}\n150: \tif err != nil {\n151: \t\ts.logger.Error(\"Querying silences failed, alerts might not get silenced correctly\", \"err\", err)\n152: \t}\n153: \tif len(allSils) == 0 {\n154: \t\t// Easy case, neither active nor pending silences anymore.\n155: \t\ts.marker.SetActiveOrSilenced(fp, newVersion, nil, nil)\n156: \t\treturn false\n157: \t}\n158: \t// It is still possible that nothing has changed, but finding out is not\n159: \t// much less effort than just recreating the IDs from the query\n160: \t// result. So let's do it in any case. Note that we cannot reuse the\n161: \t// current ID slices for concurrency reasons.\n162: \tactiveIDs, pendingIDs = nil, nil\n163: \tnow := s.silences.nowUTC()\n164: \tfor _, sil := range allSils {\n165: \t\tswitch getState(sil, now) {\n166: \t\tcase types.SilenceStatePending:\n167: \t\t\tpendingIDs = append(pendingIDs, sil.Id)\n168: \t\tcase types.SilenceStateActive:\n169: \t\t\tactiveIDs = append(activeIDs, sil.Id)\n170: \t\tdefault:\n171: \t\t\t// Do nothing, silence has expired in the meantime.\n172: \t\t}\n173: \t}\n174: \ts.logger.Debug(\n175: \t\t\"determined current silences state\",\n176: \t\t\"now\", now,\n177: \t\t\"total\", len(allSils),\n178: \t\t\"active\", len(activeIDs),\n179: \t\t\"pending\", len(pendingIDs),\n180: \t)\n181: \tsort.Strings(activeIDs)\n182: \tsort.Strings(pendingIDs)\n183: \n184: \ts.marker.SetActiveOrSilenced(fp, newVersion, activeIDs, pendingIDs)\n185: \n186: \treturn len(activeIDs) > 0\n187: }\n188: \n189: // Silences holds a silence {\n596: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n597: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n598: \n599: \tnow := s.nowUTC()\n600: \tif sil.StartsAt.IsZero() {\n601: \t\tsil.StartsAt = now\n602: \t}\n603: \n604: \tif err := Silence Check (silence/silence.go:Silencer.Mutes, line 113)**\\nThe Silencer checks if an alert is silenced by querying the Silences state. It retrieves active and pending silences matching the alert's labels. The marker tracks which silences apply to each alert. If any active silences match, Mutes returns true.\\n\\n**8. Receiver Dispatch (notify/notify.go:createReceiverStage, line 424)**\\nFor each configured receiver, createReceiverStage builds a pipeline containing:\\n- WaitStage: Waits for configured GroupWait/GroupInterval\\n- DedupStage (notify/notify.go:DedupStage, line 610): Deduplicates notifications by checking the notification log, preventing duplicate notifications based on the repeat interval\\n- RetryStage (notify/notify.go:RetryStage, line 753): Executes the actual integration notification with exponential backoff retry logic\\n- SetNotifiesStage: Logs the notification to the notification log\\n\\n**9. Final Notifier Dispatch (notify/notify.go:FanoutStage, line 488)**\\nThe FanoutStage executes all configured integrations for a receiver concurrently. Each integration's Notify() method is called to send the alert through the integration's notification channel (email, Slack, PagerDuty, etc.). The RetryStage handles exponential backoff and retry logic, with latency metrics recorded for each notification attempt.\\n\\nThe entire pipeline is orchestrated through the Stage interface and executed via MultiStage for sequential stages and FanoutStage for parallel execution.\"\n}\n",
